Malloc site tracking

The data below show the sites which do the most memory allocation, sorted by the number of mallocs in a typical run. Only sites doing 100 or more mallocs are shown. I didn't consider the size of the allocated blocks, or temporal patterns of allocation; this is pretty high-level data.

The data were generated for a single run of an optimized build of Mozilla on Mac, just bringing up a single browser window (no profile dialog), rendering a simple text-only HTML page, then quitting.

To collect the data, I added stack-walking code to the Mac's malloc implementation, which is the bottleneck for all allocations (new, malloc, calloc, realloc, and NSPR versions of same). This dumped the stack for every malloc (all 368000 of them), resulting in a 600Mb data file. With some intrepid use sort/uniq on Unix, I produced the following data.

Simon Fraser sfraser@netscape.com

	PR_Calloc
	PR_NewCondVar
	PR_Sleep
	_MD_poll
	PR_Poll
	nsSocketTransportService::Run()
	nsThread::Main(void*)
	_PR_UserRunThread
